        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192244060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10976876257561301369">I think I'm in danger of becoming a Tera-junkie. In the year 2011, I discovered her Oh.My.Gods. series and now Sweet Venom. Her easy-to-read style has carried through all of the books I've read; you open the first page and before you have a chance to breathe; you're waist deep in the story. I like that! Reading can be a learning experience with dictionary/Wikipedia look-ups required, a way to stretch your mind OR it can be a way to push everything aside while you fall into someone's story. Sweet</span>
  <span id="freeText10976876257561301369" style="display:none">I think I'm in danger of becoming a Tera-junkie. In the year 2011, I discovered her Oh.My.Gods. series and now Sweet Venom. Her easy-to-read style has carried through all of the books I've read; you open the first page and before you have a chance to breathe; you're waist deep in the story. I like that! Reading can be a learning experience with dictionary/Wikipedia look-ups required, a way to stretch your mind OR it can be a way to push everything aside while you fall into someone's story. Sweet Venom was an enjoyable journey into the meaning of sisterhood with a Greek mythological twist. <br /><br />Not familiar with the premise??? Let's fix that, shall we, with the Goodreads summary: "Grace just moved to San Francisco and is excited to start over at a new school. The change is full of fresh possibilities, but it’s also a tiny bit scary. It gets scarier when a minotaur walks in the door. And even more shocking when a girl who looks just like her shows up to fight the monster. Gretchen is tired of monsters pulling her out into the wee hours, especially on a school night, but what can she do? Sending the minotaur back to his bleak home is just another notch on her combat belt. She never expected to run into this girl who could be her double, though. <br />Greer has her life pretty well put together, thank you very much. But that all tilts sideways when two girls who look eerily like her appear on her doorstep and claim they're triplets, supernatural descendants of some hideous creature from Greek myth, destined to spend their lives hunting monsters. These three teenage descendants of Medusa, the once-beautiful gorgon maligned by myth, must reunite and embrace their fates in this unique paranormal world where monsters lurk in plain sight."<br /><br />My impressions: My teachers at school would have a field day with the nature vs nurture implications of the three separated-at-birth sisters and their vastly different lives. I, for one, just enjoyed meeting each of them. Grace, Gretchen and Greer had such different stories, viewpoints and voices that the overall book just flowed. Tera created a twist on the current mythology craze with Medusa's descendants being the ones standing between monsters and humans --- with success. I've already added book two to my TBR. This series has so many possibilities; my curosity is peaked! <br /><br />The only reason this book does not have 5 stars, cupcakes, lattes, puppies or any other measurable unit is completely subjective on my part. To earn 5 stars, the book must compel me to read it again! I really liked the story, I will buy the next installment but there was no burning drive to read it immediately upon completion...thus four stars. Should you read it? Absolutely! The three sisters have wit, humor, attitude and have stories to match.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10976876257561301369" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_172588036" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172588036" />

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172588036?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="All Things Urban Fantasy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="All Things Urban Fantasy" href="/user/show/2732683-all-things-urban-fantasy">All Things Urban Fantasy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172588036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12483527049794789741">Review courtesy of All Things Urban Fantasy<br/><br/>When I hear the word ‘Medusa’ it immediately conjures up the famous Ray Harryhausen snake haired creature from the original Clash of the Titans movie. SWEET VENOM by Tera Lynn Childs’ version bears little resemblance. Instead, she imagines teenage monster hunters who are the only ones who can see the mythological beasties that prey on humanity. No snake hair. No serpent bodies. No turning people to stone with a glance. These descendants of Medusa have l</span>
  <span id="freeText12483527049794789741" style="display:none">Review courtesy of All Things Urban Fantasy<br /><br />When I hear the word ‘Medusa’ it immediately conjures up the famous Ray Harryhausen snake haired creature from the original Clash of the Titans movie. SWEET VENOM by Tera Lynn Childs’ version bears little resemblance. Instead, she imagines teenage monster hunters who are the only ones who can see the mythological beasties that prey on humanity. No snake hair. No serpent bodies. No turning people to stone with a glance. These descendants of Medusa have lethal venom laced fangs, the ability to hypnotize with their eyes, and three powers uniquely theirs. <br /><br />Gretchen, Grace, and Greer are the three monster hunters who were separated at birth. All three do have very distinct personalities, which I appreciated, but those distinctions all kiss the cliché line more than I would like. Gretchen is the tough and jaded one who has been fighting monsters for years on her own. She’s super sarcastic and supremely unimpressed with everything. She took a long time for me to warm up to and is responsible for the less than stellar start in SWEET VENOM. Grace is the sweet, brainy sister. She’s big into computers and not so much into sticking up for herself. Greer is the sister we meet towards the end of the book. She’s the socialite snob who is more concerned with not ruining her shoes than with the monsters attacking them. <br /><br />Imagine teenaged Charmed but with Greek Mythology and you get SWEET VENOM. Not all the sisters endeared themselves to me, but the mythological ride was a fun one. I also really liked the guys in this book, two of whom clearly have big secrets they are keeping. In fact, I would have loved to read a whole book just about Grace and her mysterious older brother. Fair warning about the ending. I wouldn’t even call it a cliff hanger since the story doesn’t really get started until the end. The whole book is about the sisters finding each other, accepting their fate, and deciding to work together. The rescue mission, answers, romances, and fights will all have to wait for the next book in the Medusa Girls series which will be published in 2012. I had enough fun with this debut that I’ll be looking forward to it.<br /><br />Sexual Content:<br />References to sexual activity</span>

<div id="review_561258590" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/561258590" />
    <a title="Greta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7104111-greta"><img alt="Greta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1355520788p2/7104111.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2064653738196335551"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/>Brief Summary: Gretchen, Grace, and Greer are the mortal descendants of Medusa. Their venomous bite can send monsters back to the Abyss. This book felt very much like a first book, though. It was mostly about getting to kn</span>
  <span id="freeText2064653738196335551" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br />Brief Summary: Gretchen, Grace, and Greer are the mortal descendants of Medusa. Their venomous bite can send monsters back to the Abyss. In this book they meet, learn a little about their entwined destinies, and discover that they collectively have become the target of every beastie in town.<br /><b>Review: </b><br />I was attracted to this book because of the great concept (a reinterpretation of the Greek Medusa story). This book felt very much like a first book, though. It was mostly about getting to know the main characters, their backgrounds, and how their world is set up. There were many more questions raised then were answered, and I can’t wait to learn more about how the Greek Gods are interfering/ manipulating events in the next book. I was really left speculating.<br /><br />Told from the alternating first person perspectives of each of the girls, I liked Grace the most. All the girls had unique voices, but Grace was the most relatable to me; she was smart, level-headed and a natural peacemaker. It was actually kind of frustrating to know right from the start of the story that there would be three perspectives, but then have to read to chapter 15 before meeting one of the main characters. The boys in the story really added something, perhaps not so much in a romantic way, but I was left with so many questions about what Nick and Thane’s real backstories are and how they’ll fit in with the girls’ legacy.<br /><br />This wasn’t a riveting read, but it was a good story. Leaving off with a very exciting ending, the rest of the series has the potential to be much more interesting. It is very YA, though, I don’t think any future romance in the book will ever be fireworks-worthy.<br /><br /><b>Recommendation: </b> Yes, I’m planning to read the second one. This one is for anyone who loves YA books based on Greek myth. If you loved Starcrossed by Josephine Angelini, then this one might be worth checking out.<br /><br />For this review and others, visit my blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.fictionsnoop.com">http://www.fictionsnoop.com</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2064653738196335551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer260631581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16972587172870059349">Originally posted @ <a href='http://bookwhales.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Book Whales</a><br/><br/><br/><br/>Three sisters…<br/> One destiny…<br/><br/><br/> It’s not very often that I come across a book with three strong heroines out to fight mythological creatures that threaten humankind. All I can say is that I really enjoyed reading this book. Although the chapters were written in three different first person POV’s, it’s really easy to distinguish who’s who because each of the girls has their own distinct characteristic and voices that made them unique and Childs did such a brilliant job </span>
  <span id="freeText16972587172870059349" style="display:none">Originally posted @ <a href="http://bookwhales.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Whales</a><br><br><br><br>Three sisters…<br> One destiny…<br><br><br> It’s not very often that I come across a book with three strong heroines out to fight mythological creatures that threaten humankind. All I can say is that I really enjoyed reading this book. Although the chapters were written in three different first person POV’s, it’s really easy to distinguish who’s who because each of the girls has their own distinct characteristic and voices that made them unique and Childs did such a brilliant job writing this.<br> I love the three sisters to bits and it’s really hard choosing which one of them is my favorite. Gretchen is strong and kick-ass, Grace is sweet, caring and cheerful, while Greer is our high-class, snobby girl. Each of them has something that you can really relate to.<br> An interesting plot, awesome characters, action-packed, mythological creatures and a bit of romance, all in one book! A lot of questions were still not answered and that cliffhanger ending just made me want to read the sequel more. I can’t wait to get my hands on it!<br> I definitely recommend this to Greek mythology/YA fans!<br><br>Rating: 4.5 whales<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380367137ra/719546.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380367137ra/719546.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380367137ra/719546.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380367137ra/719546.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380367137ra/719546.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xjgk4AngOCt1s+5j773X57Y49wPwWxJy2N3iex9GdPAN1NFL5T09FbJp+6XQZaADh8ZT/WLALw6woIQJVo85gw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EQccidVX7NqaLZXGYYHitEk43zbZIDkq0rvvX03PInva6+kiOYrp5F33gABeWZVQeMZ7yEu7BFa6xoktBAZvCA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
